<p>In July 2005, all four defendants in the BALCO steroid scandal trial, including Anderson, struck deals with federal prosecutors that did not require them to reveal names of athletes who may have used banned drugs.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Perjury_case">Perjury case</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Barry_Bonds_perjury_case" title="Barry Bonds perjury case">Barry Bonds perjury case</a></div>
<p>On November 15, 2007, Bonds was indicted on four counts of <a href="/wiki/Perjury" title="Perjury">perjury</a> and one count of <a href="/wiki/Obstruction_of_justice" title="Obstruction of justice">obstruction of justice</a> as it relates to the government investigation of BALCO.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
<p>On February 14, 2008 a <a href="/wiki/Typo" class="mw-redirect" title="Typo">typo</a> in court papers filed by Federal prosecutors erroneously alleged that Bonds tested positive for steroids in November 2001, a month after hitting his record 73rd home run. The reference was meant instead to refer to a November 2000 test that had already been disclosed and previously reported.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> The typo sparked a brief media frenzy.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p>His trial for obstruction of justice was to have begun on March 2, 2009, but jury selection was postponed due to 11th-hour appeals by the prosecution.<sup id="cite_ref-deny_appeal_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deny_appeal-169">[169]</a></sup> The trial commenced on March 21, 2011, in U. S. District Court, Northern District of California, with Judge Susan Illston presiding.<sup id="cite_ref-BBgMtd_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBgMtd-170">[170]</a></sup> He was convicted on April 13, 2011 on the obstruction of justice charge, for giving an evasive answer to a question under oath.<sup id="cite_ref-latimesblogs.latimes.com_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimesblogs.latimes.com-13">[13]</a></sup> His sentence did not include prison. The conviction was initially upheld by a three judge panel of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Ninth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit">United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit</a> in 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-BBocu_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBocu-155">[155]</a></sup> but a larger panel of the court voted 10-1 to overturn the conviction on April 22, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Egelko_20150422_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Egelko_20150422-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Players.27_Union">Players' Union</span></h3>
<p>Bonds withdrew from the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Players_Association" title="Major League Baseball Players Association">MLB Players Association</a>'s (MLBPA) <a href="/wiki/License" title="License">licensing</a> agreement because he felt independent marketing deals would be more lucrative for him. Bonds is the first player in the thirty-year history of the licensing program not to sign.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> Because of this withdrawal, his name and likeness are not usable in any merchandise licensed by the MLBPA. In order to use his name or likeness, a company must deal directly with Bonds. For this reason he does not appear in some baseball <a href="/wiki/Video_games" class="mw-redirect" title="Video games">video games</a>, forcing game-makers to create generic athletes to replace him. For example, Bonds is replaced by "<a href="/wiki/Jon_Dowd" class="mw-redirect" title="Jon Dowd">Jon Dowd</a>" in <i><a href="/wiki/MVP_Baseball_2005" title="MVP Baseball 2005">MVP Baseball 2005</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_of_Shadows"><i>Game of Shadows</i></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Game_of_Shadows" title="Game of Shadows">Game of Shadows</a></div>
<p>In March 2006 the book <i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Shadows" title="Game of Shadows">Game of Shadows</a></i>, written by <a href="/wiki/Lance_Williams_and_Mark_Fainaru-Wada" title="Lance Williams and Mark Fainaru-Wada">Lance Williams and Mark Fainaru-Wada</a>, was released amid a storm of media publicity including the cover of <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> Initially small excerpts of the book were released by the authors in the issue of <i>Sports Illustrated</i>. The book alleges Bonds used <a href="/wiki/Stanozolol" title="Stanozolol">stanozolol</a> and a host of other steroids, and is perhaps most responsible for the change in public opinion regarding Bonds' steroid use.<sup id="cite_ref-TTABBaS_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TTABBaS-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<p>The book contained excerpts of grand jury testimony that is supposed to be sealed and confidential by law. The authors have been steadfast in their refusal to divulge their sources<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> and at one point faced jail time.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> On February 14, 2007, Troy Ellerman, one of <a href="/wiki/Victor_Conte" title="Victor Conte">Victor Conte</a>'s lawyers, pleaded guilty to leaking grand jury testimony. Through the plea agreement, he will spend two and a half years in jail.<sup id="cite_ref-BlEg2yip_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BlEg2yip-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Love_Me.2C_Hate_Me"><i>Love Me, Hate Me</i></span></h3>
<p>In May 2006, former <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> writer <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Pearlman" title="Jeff Pearlman">Jeff Pearlman</a> released a revealing biography of Bonds entitled <i>Love Me, Hate Me: Barry Bonds and the Making of an Anti-Hero.</i> The book also contained many allegations against Bonds.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> The book, which describes Bonds as a polarizing insufferable braggart with a legendary ego and staggering ability, relied on over five hundred interviews, except with Bonds himself.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bonds_on_Bonds"><i>Bonds on Bonds</i></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bonds_on_Bonds" title="Bonds on Bonds">Bonds on Bonds</a></div>
<p>In April 2006 and May 2006, <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> aired a few episodes of a 10-part <a href="/wiki/Reality_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Reality TV">reality TV</a> (unscripted, <a href="/wiki/Documentary_film" title="Documentary film">documentary</a>-style) series starring Bonds.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> The show, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Shows_on_ESPN#Original_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Shows on ESPN">Bonds on Bonds</a></i>, focused on Bonds' chase of <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a>'s and <a href="/wiki/Hank_Aaron" title="Hank Aaron">Hank Aaron</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">home run</a> records. Some felt the show should be put on hiatus until baseball investigated Bonds' steroid use allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> The series was canceled in June 2006, ESPN and producer Tollin/Robbins Productions citing "creative control" issues with Bonds and his representatives.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Bonds met Susann ("Sun") Margreth Branco, the mother of his first two children (Nikolai and Shikari),<sup id="cite_ref-GAsdpa_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GAsdpa-185">[185]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Montreal,_Quebec" class="mw-redirect" title="Montreal, Quebec">Montreal, Quebec</a> in August 1987. They eloped to <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a> February 5, 1988. The couple separated in June 1994, divorced in December 1994, and had their marriage <a href="/wiki/Annulment" title="Annulment">annulled</a> in 1997 by the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BaLBMP_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaLBMP-186">[186]</a></sup> The divorce was a media affair because Bonds had his Swedish spouse sign a <a href="/wiki/Prenuptial_agreement" title="Prenuptial agreement">prenuptial agreement</a> in which she "waived her right to a share of his present and future earnings" and which was upheld. Bonds had been providing his wife $20,000/month in child support and $10,000 in spousal support at the time of the ruling.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> During the hearings to set permanent support levels, allegations of abuse came from both parties.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> The trial dragged on for months, but Bonds was awarded both houses and reduced support.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> On August 21, 2000, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_California" title="Supreme Court of California">Supreme Court of California</a>, in an opinion signed by Chief Justice <a href="/wiki/Ronald_M._George" title="Ronald M. George">Ronald M. George</a>, unanimously held that "substantial evidence supports the determination of the trial court that the [prenuptial] agreement in the present case was entered into voluntarily."<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> In reaction to the decision,<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> significant changes in California law relating to the validity and enforceability of premarital agreements soon followed.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, Bonds' son Nikolai, who served as a Giants <a href="/wiki/Batboy" title="Batboy">batboy</a> during his father's years playing in San Francisco and always sat next to his dad in the dugout during games,<sup id="cite_ref-batboyson_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batboyson-195">[195]</a></sup> was charged with five <a href="/wiki/Misdemeanor" title="Misdemeanor">misdemeanors</a> resulting from a confrontation with his mother, Sun. Barry accompanied him to San Mateo County Superior Court.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the end of his first marriage, Bonds had an extensive intimate relationship with Kimberly Bell from 1994 through May 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> Bonds purchased a home in <a href="/wiki/Scottsdale,_Arizona" title="Scottsdale, Arizona">Scottsdale, Arizona</a> for Kimberly.<sup id="cite_ref-BaLBMP_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaLBMP-186">[186]</a></sup></p>
<p>On January 10, 1998, Bonds married his second wife, Liz Watson, at the San Francisco <a href="/wiki/Ritz-Carlton" class="mw-redirect" title="Ritz-Carlton">Ritz-Carlton</a> Hotel in front of 240 guests.<sup id="cite_ref-BaLBMP_186-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaLBMP-186">[186]</a></sup> The couple lived in <a href="/wiki/Los_Altos_Hills,_California" title="Los Altos Hills, California">Los Altos Hills, California</a>, with their daughter Aisha<sup id="cite_ref-BaLBMP_186-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaLBMP-186">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SecondWife_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SecondWife-198">[198]</a></sup> during their ten and a half years of marriage before Watson filed for Legal Separation on June 9, 2009, citing <a href="/wiki/Irreconcilable_differences" title="Irreconcilable differences">irreconcilable differences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> On July 21, 2009, just six weeks later, Watson announced that she was withdrawing her Legal Separation action.<sup id="cite_ref-Reconciliation_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reconciliation-200">[200]</a></sup> The couple were reconciled for seven months before Watson formally filed for divorce in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> on February 26, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-WatsonDivorce_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WatsonDivorce-201">[201]</a></sup> On June 6, 2011, Bonds and Watson filed a legal agreement not to take the divorce to trial and instead settle it in an "uncontested manner", effectively agreeing to take the proceedings out of the public eye and end the marriage privately at an unspecified later date without further court involvement.<sup id="cite_ref-UncontestedManner_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UncontestedManner-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several of Bonds' family and extended family members have been involved in athletics as either a career or a notable pastime. Bonds has a younger brother, <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Bonds,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Bobby Bonds, Jr.">Bobby, Jr.</a>, who was also a professional baseball player.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> His paternal aunt, <a href="/wiki/Rosie_Bonds" title="Rosie Bonds">Rosie Bonds</a>, is a former American record holder in the 80 meter <a href="/wiki/Hurdles" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurdles">hurdles</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> and competed in the 1964 Olympics.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> In addition, he is a distant cousin of Hall of Famer <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Jackson" title="Reggie Jackson">Reggie Jackson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBEB_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBEB-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Among Bonds' many real estate properties is a home he owns in the exclusive gated community of <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Beverly Park">Beverly Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Hills" class="mw-redirect" title="Beverly Hills">Beverly Hills</a>, California.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup></p>
<p>An avid <a href="/wiki/Cyclist" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyclist">cyclist</a>, the activity became one of Bonds' primary means of keeping in shape and great passion since his playing career. Because of knee surgeries, back surgeries and hip surgeries making it much more difficult to run, cycling has allowed him to engage in sufficient cardiovascular activity to help keep in shape. As a result of the cycling, he has lost 25 pounds from his final playing weight of 240 pounds.<sup id="cite_ref-moore060116_159-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moore060116-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_distinctions">Career distinctions</span></h2>
<p>Besides holding Major League career records in home runs (762), walks (2,558), and intentional walks (688), at the time of his retirement, Bonds also led all active players in RBI (1,996), <a href="/wiki/On-base_percentage" title="On-base percentage">on-base percentage</a> (.444), runs (2,227), games (2,986), extra-base hits (1,440), at-bats per home run (12.92), and <a href="/wiki/Total_bases" class="mw-redirect" title="Total bases">total bases</a> (5,976). He is 2nd in doubles (601), slugging percentage (.607), stolen bases (514), at-bats (9,847), and hits (2,935), 6th in triples (77), 8th in sacrifice flies (91), and 9th in <a href="/wiki/Strikeout" title="Strikeout">strikeouts</a> (1,539), through September 26, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_19-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bonds is the lone member of the 500–500 club, which means he has hit at least 500 home runs (762) and stolen 500 bases (514). He is also one of only four baseball players all-time to be in the 40–40 club (1996), which means he hit 40 home runs (42) and stole 40 bases (40) in the same season; the other members are <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Canseco" class="mw-redirect" title="José Canseco">José Canseco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez" title="Alex Rodriguez">Alex Rodriguez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Soriano" title="Alfonso Soriano">Alfonso Soriano</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Records_held">Records held</span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Barry_Bonds&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(March 2017)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Progression_of_the_single-season_MLB_home_run_record" class="mw-redirect" title="Progression of the single-season MLB home run record">Home runs in a single season</a> (73), 2001</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_lifetime_home_run_leaders_in_Major_League_Baseball" class="mw-redirect" title="List of lifetime home run leaders in Major League Baseball">Home runs (career)</a> (762)</li>
<li>Home runs against different pitchers (449)</li>
<li>Home runs since turning 40 years old (74)</li>
<li>Home runs in the year he turned 43 years old (28)</li>
<li>Consecutive seasons with 30 or more home runs (13), 1992–2004</li>
<li>Slugging percentage in a single season (.863), 2001</li>
<li>Slugging percentage in a World Series (1.294), 2002</li>
<li>Consecutive seasons with .600 slugging percentage or higher (8), 1998–2005</li>
<li>On-base percentage in a single season (.609), 2004</li>
<li>Walks in a single season (232), 2004</li>
<li>Intentional walks in a single season (120), 2004</li>
<li>Consecutive games with a walk (18)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Major League Baseball Most Valuable Player Award">MVP</a> awards (7—closest competitors trail with 3), 1990, 1992–93, 2001–04</li>
<li>Consecutive MVP awards (4), 2001–04</li>
<li>National League <a href="/wiki/Player_of_the_Month" class="mw-redirect" title="Player of the Month">Player of the Month</a> selections (13—2nd place: 8 – <a href="/wiki/Frank_Thomas_(designated_hitter)" title="Frank Thomas (designated hitter)">Frank Thomas</a>; 2nd place (N.L.) – <a href="/wiki/George_Foster_(baseball)" title="George Foster (baseball)">George Foster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pete_Rose" title="Pete Rose">Pete Rose</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dale_Murphy" title="Dale Murphy">Dale Murphy</a>)</li>
<li>Oldest player (age 38) to win the National League <a href="/wiki/Batting_average" title="Batting average">batting title</a> (.370) for the first time, 2002</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Records_shared">Records shared</span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Consecutive plate appearances with a walk (7)</li>
<li>Consecutive plate appearances reaching base (15)<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></li>
<li>Tied with his father, Bobby, for most seasons with 30 home runs and 30 stolen bases (5) and are the only father-son members of the 30–30 club</li>
<li>Home runs in a single post-season (8), 2002</li>
</ul>

<td></td>

<td><a href="/wiki/Silver_Slugger_Award" title="Silver Slugger Award">Silver Slugger Award</a> at outfield</td>
<td align="center">12</td>
<td>1990–94, 1996–97, 2000–04</td>
<td></td>
</tr>
</table>
<ul>
<li>5-time SF Giants Player of the Year (1998, 2001–04)</li>
<li>3-Time NL Hank Aaron Award winner (2001–02, 2004)</li>
<li>Listed at #6 on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sporting_News" class="mw-redirect" title="The Sporting News">The Sporting News</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span> list of the 100 Greatest Baseball Players, the highest-ranked active player, i n 2005.</li>
<li>Named a finalist to the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Century_Team" title="Major League Baseball All-Century Team">Major League Baseball All-Century Team</a> in 1999, but not elected to the team in the fan balloting.</li>
<li>Rating of 352 on Baseball-Reference.com's Hall of Fame monitor (100 is a good HOF candidate);<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> 9th among all hitters, highest among hitters not in HOF yet.</li>
<li>Only the second player to twice have a single-season slugging percentage over .800, with his record .863 in 2001 and .812 in 2004. Babe Ruth was the other, with .847 in 1920 and .846 in 1921.</li>
<li>Became the first player in history with more times on base (376) than official times at bats (373) in 2004. This was due to the record number of walks, which count as a time on base but not a time at-bat. He had 135 hits, 232 walks, and 9 hit-by-pitches for the 376 number.</li>
<li>With his father <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Bonds" title="Bobby Bonds">Bobby</a> (332, 461), leads all father-son combinations in combined home runs (1,094) and stolen bases (975), respectively through September 26, 2007.</li>
<li>Played minor league baseball in both Alaska and Hawaii. In 1983, he played for the Alaska Goldpanners of Fairbanks in the Alaska Baseball League,<sup id="cite_ref-TAGoF_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TAGoF-22">[22]</a></sup> and in 1986, he played for the Hawaii Islanders in the Pacific Coast League.</li>
<li>Featured on the cover of <a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> He has appeared as the main subject on the cover eight times in total; seven with the Giants and once with the Pirates. He has also appeared in an inset on the cover twice. He was the most recent Pirate player to appear on the cover,<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> until Jason Grilli was featured in SIs edition of July 22, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
